```python
'''
Main application file for handling coding challenges.
'''
from tkinter import Tk, Label, Entry, Button, Text, Scrollbar, END
from challenge_handler import ChallengeHandler
from database_manager import DatabaseManager

class MainApp:
    def __init__(self):
        self.db_manager = DatabaseManager()
        self.window = Tk()
        self.window.title("Coding Challenge Handler")
        Label(self.window, text="Enter Coding Challenge:").pack()
        self.challenge_input = Text(self.window, height=10, width=50)
        self.challenge_input.pack()
        Label(self.window, text="Select Language (Python/JavaScript):").pack()
        self.language_input = Entry(self.window)
        self.language_input.pack()
        self.submit_button = Button(self.window, text="Submit", command=self.submit_challenge)
        self.submit_button.pack()
        self.result_area = Text(self.window, height=10, width=50)
        self.result_area.pack()
        self.clear_button = Button(self.window, text="Clear", command=self.clear_input)
        self.clear_button.pack()
        self.window.protocol("WM_DELETE_WINDOW", self.on_closing)
        self.window.mainloop()

    def submit_challenge(self):
        challenge = self.challenge_input.get("1.0", END).strip()
        language = self.language_input.get().strip()
        handler = ChallengeHandler(language)
        result = handler.execute_challenge(challenge)
        self.result_area.delete("1.0", END)
        self.result_area.insert(END, result)
        self.db_manager.save_challenge(challenge)  # Save challenge to the database

    def clear_input(self):
        self.challenge_input.delete("1.0", END)
        self.language_input.delete(0, END)
        self.result_area.delete("1.0", END)

    def on_closing(self):
        self.db_manager.close()  # Close database connection on exit
        self.window.destroy()

if __name__ == "__main__":
    MainApp()

challenge_handler.py
```python
'''
Handles the execution of coding challenges based on the selected programming language.
'''
try:
    import execjs
except ImportError:
    raise ImportError("The 'execjs' module is required for JavaScript execution. Please install it using 'pip install PyExecJS'.")

class ChallengeHandler:
    def __init__(self, language):
        self.language = language.lower()

    def execute_challenge(self, challenge):
        if self.language == "python":
            return self.execute_python(challenge)
        elif self.language == "javascript":
            return self.execute_javascript(challenge)
        else:
            return "Unsupported language."

    def execute_python(self, challenge):
        try:
            exec_globals = {}
            exec(challenge, exec_globals)
            return "Python challenge executed successfully."
        except Exception as e:
            return f"Error executing Python challenge: {str(e)}"

    def execute_javascript(self, challenge):
        '''
        Executes the provided JavaScript challenge code.
        Assumes the JavaScript code contains a function named 'main' to be called.
        '''
        try:
            context = execjs.compile(challenge)
            # Check if the 'main' function exists in the JavaScript code
            if 'main' not in context.call('get_functions')():  # Assuming a method to get function names
                return "Error: JavaScript code must contain a 'main' function."
            context.call('main')  # Assuming the JavaScript code has a main function
            return "JavaScript challenge executed successfully."
        except Exception as e:
            return f"Error executing JavaScript challenge: {str(e)}"
```

database_manager.py
```python
'''
Manages database interactions for saving and retrieving coding challenges.
'''
import sqlite3

class DatabaseManager:
    def __init__(self):
        # Initialize database connection here
        self.connection = sqlite3.connect('challenges.db')
        self.create_table()

    def create_table(self):
        # Create a table for storing coding challenges if it doesn't exist
        with self.connection:
            self.connection.execute('''
                CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS challenges (
                    id INTEGER PRIMARY KEY AUTOINCREMENT,
                    challenge TEXT NOT NULL
                )
            ''')

    def save_challenge(self, challenge):
        # Logic to save challenge to the database
        with self.connection:
            self.connection.execute('INSERT INTO challenges (challenge) VALUES (?)', (challenge,))

    def retrieve_challenges(self):
        # Logic to retrieve challenges from the database
        cursor = self.connection.cursor()
        cursor.execute('SELECT challenge FROM challenges')
        return cursor.fetchall()

    def close(self):
        # Close the database connection
        self.connection.close()
```

challenge_handler.py
```python
'''
Handles the execution of coding challenges based on the selected programming language.
'''
try:
    import execjs
except ImportError:
    raise ImportError("The 'execjs' module is required for JavaScript execution. Please install it using 'pip install PyExecJS'.")

class ChallengeHandler:
    def __init__(self, language):
        self.language = language.lower()

    def execute_challenge(self, challenge):
        if self.language == "python":
            return self.execute_python(challenge)
        elif self.language == "javascript":
            return self.execute_javascript(challenge)
        else:
            return "Unsupported language."

    def execute_python(self, challenge):
        try:
            exec_globals = {}
            exec(challenge, exec_globals)
            return "Python challenge executed successfully."
        except Exception as e:
            return f"Error executing Python challenge: {str(e)}"

    def execute_javascript(self, challenge):
        '''
        Executes the provided JavaScript challenge code.
        Assumes the JavaScript code contains a function named 'main' to be called.
        '''
        try:
            context = execjs.compile(challenge)
            # Check if the 'main' function exists in the JavaScript code
            if 'main' not in context.call('get_functions')():  # Assuming a method to get function names
                return "Error: JavaScript code must contain a 'main' function."
            context.call('main')  # Assuming the JavaScript code has a main function
            return "JavaScript challenge executed successfully."
        except Exception as e:
            return f"Error executing JavaScript challenge: {str(e)}"

'''

import sqlite3

class DatabaseManager:
    def __init__(self):
        # Initialize database connection here
        self.connection = sqlite3.connect('challenges.db')
        self.create_table()

    def create_table(self):
        # Create a table for storing coding challenges if it doesn't exist
        with self.connection:
            self.connection.execute('''
                CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS challenges (
                    id INTEGER PRIMARY KEY AUTOINCREMENT,
                    challenge TEXT NOT NULL
                )
            ''')

    def save_challenge(self, challenge):
        # Logic to save challenge to the database
        with self.connection:
            self.connection.execute('INSERT INTO challenges (challenge) VALUES (?)', (challenge,))

    def retrieve_challenges(self):
        # Logic to retrieve challenges from the database
        cursor = self.connection.cursor()
        cursor.execute('SELECT challenge FROM challenges')
        return cursor.fetchall()

    def close(self):
        # Close the database connection
        self.connection.close()

challenge_handler.py
```python
'''
Handles the execution of coding challenges based on the selected programming language.
'''
import execjs
class ChallengeHandler:
    def __init__(self, language):
        self.language = language.lower()
    def execute_challenge(self, challenge):
        if self.language == "python":
            return self.execute_python(challenge)
        elif self.language == "javascript":
            return self.execute_javascript(challenge)
        else:
            return "Unsupported language."
    def execute_python(self, challenge):
        try:
            exec_globals = {}
            exec(challenge, exec_globals)
            return "Python challenge executed successfully."
        except Exception as e:
            return f"Error executing Python challenge: {str(e)}"
    def execute_javascript(self, challenge):
        '''
        Executes the provided JavaScript challenge code.
        Assumes the JavaScript code contains a function named 'main' to be called.
        '''
        try:
            context = execjs.compile(challenge)
            # Check if the 'main' function exists in the JavaScript code
            if 'main' not in context.call('get_functions')():  # Assuming a method to get function names
                return "Error: JavaScript code must contain a 'main' function."
            context.call('main')  # Assuming the JavaScript code has a main function
            return "JavaScript challenge executed successfully."
        except Exception as e:
            return f"Error executing JavaScript challenge: {str(e)}"

database_manager.py
```python
'''
Manages database interactions for saving and retrieving coding challenges.
'''
import sqlite3
class DatabaseManager:
    def __init__(self):
        # Initialize database connection here
        self.connection = sqlite3.connect('challenges.db')
        self.create_table()
    def create_table(self):
        # Create a table for storing coding challenges if it doesn't exist
        with self.connection:
            self.connection.execute('''
                CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS challenges (
                    id INTEGER PRIMARY KEY AUTOINCREMENT,
                    challenge TEXT NOT NULL
                )
            ''')
    def save_challenge(self, challenge):
        # Logic to save challenge to the database
        with self.connection:
            self.connection.execute('INSERT INTO challenges (challenge) VALUES (?)', (challenge,))
    def retrieve_challenges(self):
        # Logic to retrieve challenges from the database
        cursor = self.connection.cursor()
        cursor.execute('SELECT challenge FROM challenges')
        return cursor.fetchall()
    def close(self):
        # Close the database connection
        self.connection.close()

main.py
```python
'''
Main application file for handling coding challenges.
'''
from tkinter import Tk, Label, Entry, Button, Text, Scrollbar, END
from challenge_handler import ChallengeHandler
from database_manager import DatabaseManager

class MainApp:
    def __init__(self):
        self.db_manager = DatabaseManager()
        self.window = Tk()
        self.window.title("Coding Challenge Handler")
        Label(self.window, text="Enter Coding Challenge:").pack()
        self.challenge_input = Text(self.window, height=10, width=50)
        self.challenge_input.pack()
        Label(self.window, text="Select Language (Python/JavaScript):").pack()
        self.language_input = Entry(self.window)
        self.language_input.pack()
        self.submit_button = Button(self.window, text="Submit", command=self.submit_challenge)
        self.submit_button.pack()
        self.result_area = Text(self.window, height=10, width=50)
        self.result_area.pack()
        self.clear_button = Button(self.window, text="Clear", command=self.clear_input)
        self.clear_button.pack()
        self.window.protocol("WM_DELETE_WINDOW", self.on_closing)
        self.window.mainloop()

    def submit_challenge(self):
        challenge = self.challenge_input.get("1.0", END).strip()
        language = self.language_input.get().strip()
        handler = ChallengeHandler(language)
        result = handler.execute_challenge(challenge)
        self.result_area.delete("1.0", END)
        self.result_area.insert(END, result)
        self.db_manager.save_challenge(challenge)  # Save challenge to the database

    def clear_input(self):
        self.challenge_input.delete("1.0", END)
        self.language_input.delete(0, END)
        self.result_area.delete("1.0", END)

    def on_closing(self):
        self.db_manager.close()  # Close database connection on exit
        self.window.destroy()

if __name__ == "__main__":
    MainApp()
```

challenge_handler.py
```python
'''
Handles the execution of coding challenges based on the selected programming language.
'''
try:
    import execjs
except ImportError:
    raise ImportError("The 'execjs' module is required. Please install it using 'pip install PyExecJS'.")

class ChallengeHandler:
    def __init__(self, language):
        self.language = language.lower()

    def execute_challenge(self, challenge):
        if self.language == "python":
            return self.execute_python(challenge)
        elif self.language == "javascript":
            return self.execute_javascript(challenge)
        else:
            return "Unsupported language."

    def execute_python(self, challenge):
        try:
            exec_globals = {}
            exec(challenge, exec_globals)
            return "Python challenge executed successfully."
        except Exception as e:
            return f"Error executing Python challenge: {str(e)}"

    def execute_javascript(self, challenge):
        '''
        Executes the provided JavaScript challenge code.
        Assumes the JavaScript code contains a function named 'main' to be called.
        '''
        try:
            context = execjs.compile(challenge)
            # Check if the 'main' function exists in the JavaScript code
            if 'main' not in context.call('get_functions')():  # Assuming a method to get function names
                return "Error: JavaScript code must contain a 'main' function."
            context.call('main')  # Assuming the JavaScript code has a main function
            return "JavaScript challenge executed successfully."
        except Exception as e:
            return f"Error executing JavaScript challenge: {str(e)}"
```

database_manager.py
```python
'''
Manages database interactions for saving and retrieving coding challenges.
'''
import sqlite3

class DatabaseManager:
    def __init__(self):
        # Initialize database connection here
        self.connection = sqlite3.connect('challenges.db')
        self.create_table()

    def create_table(self):
        # Create a table for storing coding challenges if it doesn't exist
        with self.connection:
            self.connection.execute('''
                CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS challenges (
                    id INTEGER PRIMARY KEY AUTOINCREMENT,
                    challenge TEXT NOT NULL
                )
            ''')

    def save_challenge(self, challenge):
        # Logic to save challenge to the database
        with self.connection:
            self.connection.execute('INSERT INTO challenges (challenge) VALUES (?)', (challenge,))

    def retrieve_challenges(self):
        # Logic to retrieve challenges from the database
        cursor = self.connection.cursor()
        cursor.execute('SELECT challenge FROM challenges')
        return cursor.fetchall()

    def close(self):
        # Close the database connection
        self.connection.close()
```

'''
Handles the execution of coding challenges based on the selected programming language.
'''
import execjs
class ChallengeHandler:
    def __init__(self, language):
        self.language = language.lower()
    def execute_challenge(self, challenge):
        if self.language == "python":
            return self.execute_python(challenge)
        elif self.language == "javascript":
            return self.execute_javascript(challenge)
        else:
            return "Unsupported language."
    def execute_python(self, challenge):
        try:
            exec_globals = {}
            exec(challenge, exec_globals)
            return "Python challenge executed successfully."
        except Exception as e:
            return f"Error executing Python challenge: {str(e)}"
    def execute_javascript(self, challenge):
        '''
        Executes the provided JavaScript challenge code.
        Assumes the JavaScript code contains a function named 'main' to be called.
        '''
        try:
            context = execjs.compile(challenge)
            # Check if the 'main' function exists in the JavaScript code
            if 'main' not in context.call('get_functions')():  # Assuming a method to get function names
                return "Error: JavaScript code must contain a 'main' function."
            context.call('main')  # Assuming the JavaScript code has a main function
            return "JavaScript challenge executed successfully."
        except Exception as e:
            return f"Error executing JavaScript challenge: {str(e)}"

'''

import sqlite3
class DatabaseManager:
    def __init__(self):
        # Initialize database connection here
        self.connection = sqlite3.connect('challenges.db')
        self.create_table()
    def create_table(self):
        # Create a table for storing coding challenges if it doesn't exist
        with self.connection:
            self.connection.execute('''
                CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS challenges (
                    id INTEGER PRIMARY KEY AUTOINCREMENT,
                    challenge TEXT NOT NULL
                )
            ''')
    def save_challenge(self, challenge):
        # Logic to save challenge to the database
        with self.connection:
            self.connection.execute('INSERT INTO challenges (challenge) VALUES (?)', (challenge,))
    def retrieve_challenges(self):
        # Logic to retrieve challenges from the database
        cursor = self.connection.cursor()
        cursor.execute('SELECT challenge FROM challenges')
        return cursor.fetchall()
    def close(self):
        # Close the database connection
        self.connection.close()

"main.py
```python
'''
Main application file for handling coding challenges.
'''
from tkinter import Tk, Label, Entry, Button, Text, Scrollbar, END
from challenge_handler import ChallengeHandler
from database_manager import DatabaseManager
class MainApp:
    def __init__(self):
        self.db_manager = DatabaseManager()
        self.window = Tk()
        self.window.title("Coding Challenge Handler")
        Label(self.window, text="Enter Coding Challenge:").pack()
        self.challenge_input = Text(self.window, height=10, width=50)
        self.challenge_input.pack()
        Label(self.window, text="Select Language (Python/JavaScript):").pack()
        self.language_input = Entry(self.window)
        self.language_input.pack()
        self.submit_button = Button(self.window, text="Submit", command=self.submit_challenge)
        self.submit_button.pack()
        self.result_area = Text(self.window, height=10, width=50)
        self.result_area.pack()
        self.clear_button = Button(self.window, text="Clear", command=self.clear_input)
        self.clear_button.pack()
        self.window.protocol("WM_DELETE_WINDOW", self.on_closing)
        self.window.mainloop()
    def submit_challenge(self):
        challenge = self.challenge_input.get("1.0", END).strip()
        language = self.language_input.get().strip()
        handler = ChallengeHandler(language)
        result = handler.execute_challenge(challenge)
        self.result_area.delete("1.0", END)
        self.result_area.insert(END, result)
        self.db_manager.save_challenge(challenge)  # Save challenge to the database
    def clear_input(self):
        self.challenge_input.delete("1.0", END)
        self.language_input.delete(0, END)
        self.result_area.delete("1.0", END)
    def on_closing(self):
        self.db_manager.close()  # Close database connection on exit
        self.window.destroy()
if __name__ == "__main__":
    MainApp()
```
challenge_handler.py
```python
'''
Handles the execution of coding challenges based on the selected programming language.
'''
import execjs
class ChallengeHandler:
    def __init__(self, language):
        self.language = language.lower()
    def execute_challenge(self, challenge):
        if self.language == "python":
            return self.execute_python(challenge)
        elif self.language == "javascript":
            return self.execute_javascript(challenge)
        else:
            return "Unsupported language."
    def execute_python(self, challenge):
        try:
            exec_globals = {}
            exec(challenge, exec_globals)
            return "Python challenge executed successfully."
        except Exception as e:
            return f"Error executing Python challenge: {str(e)}"
    def execute_javascript(self, challenge):
        '''
        Executes the provided JavaScript challenge code.
        Assumes the JavaScript code contains a function named 'main' to be called.
        '''
        try:
            context = execjs.compile(challenge)
            # Check if the 'main' function exists in the JavaScript code
            if 'main' not in context.call('get_functions')():  # Assuming a method to get function names
                return "Error: JavaScript code must contain a 'main' function."
            context.call('main')  # Assuming the JavaScript code has a main function
            return "JavaScript challenge executed successfully."
        except Exception as e:
            return f"Error executing JavaScript challenge: {str(e)}"
```
database_manager.py
```python
'''
Manages database interactions for saving and retrieving coding challenges.
'''
import sqlite3
class DatabaseManager:
    def __init__(self):
        # Initialize database connection here
        self.connection = sqlite3.connect('challenges.db')
        self.create_table()
    def create_table(self):
        # Create a table for storing coding challenges if it doesn't exist
        with self.connection:
            self.connection.execute('''
                CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS challenges (
                    id INTEGER PRIMARY KEY AUTOINCREMENT,
                    challenge TEXT NOT NULL
                )
            ''')
    def save_challenge(self, challenge):
        # Logic to save challenge to the database
        with self.connection:
            self.connection.execute('INSERT INTO challenges (challenge) VALUES (?)', (challenge,))
    def retrieve_challenges(self):
        # Logic to retrieve challenges from the database
        cursor = self.connection.cursor()
        cursor.execute('SELECT challenge FROM challenges')
        return cursor.fetchall()
    def close(self):
        # Close the database connection
        self.connection.close()
```

"main.py
```python
'''
Main application file for handling coding challenges.
'''
from tkinter import Tk, Label, Entry, Button, Text, Scrollbar, END
from challenge_handler import ChallengeHandler
from database_manager import DatabaseManager
class MainApp:
    def __init__(self):
        self.db_manager = DatabaseManager()
        self.window = Tk()
        self.window.title("Coding Challenge Handler")
        Label(self.window, text="Enter Coding Challenge:").pack()
        self.challenge_input = Text(self.window, height=10, width=50)
        self.challenge_input.pack()
        Label(self.window, text="Select Language (Python/JavaScript):").pack()
        self.language_input = Entry(self.window)
        self.language_input.pack()
        self.submit_button = Button(self.window, text="Submit", command=self.submit_challenge)
        self.submit_button.pack()
        self.result_area = Text(self.window, height=10, width=50)
        self.result_area.pack()
        self.clear_button = Button(self.window, text="Clear", command=self.clear_input)
        self.clear_button.pack()
        self.window.protocol("WM_DELETE_WINDOW", self.on_closing)
        self.window.mainloop()
    def submit_challenge(self):
        challenge = self.challenge_input.get("1.0", END).strip()
        language = self.language_input.get().strip()
        handler = ChallengeHandler(language)
        result = handler.execute_challenge(challenge)
        self.result_area.delete("1.0", END)
        self.result_area.insert(END, result)
        self.db_manager.save_challenge(challenge)  # Save challenge to the database
    def clear_input(self):
        self.challenge_input.delete("1.0", END)
        self.language_input.delete(0, END)
        self.result_area.delete("1.0", END)
    def on_closing(self):
        self.db_manager.close()  # Close database connection on exit
        self.window.destroy()
if __name__ == "__main__":
    MainApp()
```

challenge_handler.py
```python
'''
Handles the execution of coding challenges based on the selected programming language.
'''
import execjs
class ChallengeHandler:
    def __init__(self, language):
        self.language = language.lower()
    def execute_challenge(self, challenge):
        if self.language == "python":
            return self.execute_python(challenge)
        elif self.language == "javascript":
            return self.execute_javascript(challenge)
        else:
            return "Unsupported language."
    def execute_python(self, challenge):
        try:
            exec_globals = {}
            exec(challenge, exec_globals)
            return "Python challenge executed successfully."
        except Exception as e:
            return f"Error executing Python challenge: {str(e)}"
    def execute_javascript(self, challenge):
        '''
        Executes the provided JavaScript challenge code.
        Assumes the JavaScript code contains a function named 'main' to be called.
        '''
        try:
            context = execjs.compile(challenge)
            # Check if the 'main' function exists in the JavaScript code
            if 'main' not in context.call('get_functions')():  # Assuming a method to get function names
                return "Error: JavaScript code must contain a 'main' function."
            context.call('main')  # Assuming the JavaScript code has a main function
            return "JavaScript challenge executed successfully."
        except Exception as e:
            return f"Error executing JavaScript challenge: {str(e)}"
```

database_manager.py
```python
'''
Manages database interactions for saving and retrieving coding challenges.
'''
import sqlite3
class DatabaseManager:
    def __init__(self):
        # Initialize database connection here
        self.connection = sqlite3.connect('challenges.db')
        self.create_table()
    def create_table(self):
        # Create a table for storing coding challenges if it doesn't exist
        with self.connection:
            self.connection.execute('''
                CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS challenges (
                    id INTEGER PRIMARY KEY AUTOINCREMENT,
                    challenge TEXT NOT NULL
                )
            ''')
    def save_challenge(self, challenge):
        # Logic to save challenge to the database
        with self.connection:
            self.connection.execute('INSERT INTO challenges (challenge) VALUES (?)', (challenge,))
    def retrieve_challenges(self):
        # Logic to retrieve challenges from the database
        cursor = self.connection.cursor()
        cursor.execute('SELECT challenge FROM challenges')
        return cursor.fetchall()
    def close(self):
        # Close the database connection
        self.connection.close()
```

# LangChain

Building applications with LLMs through composability

Looking for the JS/TS version? Check out LangChain.js.

**Production Support:** As you move your LangChains into production, we'd love to offer more comprehensive support.

Please fill out this form and we'll set up a dedicated support Slack channel.

## Quick Install

`pip install langchain`

or

`conda install langchain -c conda-forge`

## 🤔 What is this?

Large language models (LLMs) are emerging as a transformative technology, enabling developers to build applications that they previously could not. However, using these LLMs in isolation is often insufficient for creating a truly powerful app - the real power comes when you can combine them with other sources of computation or knowledge.

This library aims to assist in the development of those types of applications. Common examples of these applications include:

**❓ Question Answering over specific documents**

- Documentation

- End-to-end Example: Question Answering over Notion Database

**🤖 Agents**

- Documentation

- End-to-end Example: GPT+WolframAlpha

## 📖 Documentation

Please see [here](https://python.langchain.com) for full documentation on:

- Getting started (installation, setting up the environment, simple examples)

- How-To examples (demos, integrations, helper functions)

- Reference (full API docs)

- Resources (high-level explanation of core concepts)

```markdown
# Coding Challenge Handler

A systematic application for handling intermediate-level coding challenges in Python and JavaScript/React, with a focus on maintaining a consistent turnaround time and thorough documentation.

## Main Functions

- **Submit Coding Challenges**: Users can input coding challenges in either Python or JavaScript and execute them.
- **Database Management**: The application saves submitted challenges to a SQLite database for future reference.
- **Clear Input**: Users can easily clear the input fields to start fresh.
- **Error Handling**: The application provides feedback on execution errors for both Python and JavaScript challenges.

## Quick Install

To run the Coding Challenge Handler, you need to install the required dependencies. Follow the steps below:

1. **Install Python**: Ensure you have Python installed on your machine. You can download it from [python.org](https://www.python.org/downloads/).

2. **Install Required Packages**: Open your terminal or command prompt and run the following command to install the necessary packages:

   ```bash
   pip install execjs
   ```

3. **Set Up SQLite**: SQLite comes pre-installed with Python, so you don't need to install it separately.

## 🤔 What is this?

The Coding Challenge Handler is designed to help developers practice and execute coding challenges in a user-friendly environment. It supports both Python and JavaScript, allowing users to test their skills and receive immediate feedback on their code.

## 📖 How to Use

1. **Run the Application**: Execute the `main.py` file to launch the application. You can do this by navigating to the directory where the file is located and running:

   ```bash
   python main.py
   ```

2. **Input Coding Challenge**: In the application window, enter your coding challenge in the provided text area.

3. **Select Language**: Specify the programming language (either `Python` or `JavaScript`) in the input field.

4. **Submit Challenge**: Click the "Submit" button to execute the challenge. The result will be displayed in the result area.

5. **Clear Input**: If you want to start over, click the "Clear" button to reset the input fields.

6. **Database Interaction**: All submitted challenges will be saved to the `challenges.db` SQLite database for future reference.

7. **Close Application**: When you are done, simply close the application window. The database connection will be closed automatically.

## Error Handling

- If you encounter an error while executing a Python challenge, the application will display an error message indicating the issue.
- For JavaScript challenges, ensure that your code contains a `main` function, as the application expects to call this function during execution.

## Conclusion

The Coding Challenge Handler is a powerful tool for developers looking to improve their coding skills in Python and JavaScript. With its easy-to-use interface and robust functionality, you can practice coding challenges efficiently and effectively.

For further assistance or support, please reach out to our development team.
```
